Since returning to the US in 1982, he has written shuttle navigation software, a software support environment prototype, and supported strategic information planning, all at NASA’s Johnson Space Center. After a two-year stint at full-time writing, he’s back at NASA developing shuttle navigation software.

Jonathan Osuch started throwing pebbles into the soup around version 15.0 with a method for simulating an if-then-else structure using the formula parser. He has contributed the fn||fn fractal types, the built- in bailout tests, the increase in both the maximum iteration count and bailout value, and bug fixes too numerous to count. Jonathan worked closely with Robin Bussell to implement Robin’s browser mechanism in Fractint.

Jonathan has a B.S. in Physics from the University of Dubuque and a B.S. in Computer Science from Mount Mercy College, both in Iowa. He is currently working as a consultant in the nuclear power industry.

Wes Loewer first got his foot in the Stone Soup door by writing fast floating point assembler routines for Mandelbrot, Julia, and Lyapunov fractals. He also rewrote the boundary trace algorithms and added the frothybasin fractal. His most significant contribution is the addition of the arbitrary precision library which allows Fractint to perform incredibly deep zooms.

Wes has a B.S. in Physics from Wheaton College in Illinois. He also holds an M.S. in Physics and an M.Ed. in Education from Texas A&M University. Wes teaches physics and math at McCullough High School in The Woodlands, Texas where his pupils inspire him to keep that sense of amazement that students get when they understand a physical or mathematical principle for the first time. Since he uses Fractint to help teach certain mathematical principles, he’s one of the few folks who actually gets to use Fractint on the job. Besides his involvement with Fractint, Wes is the author of WL-Plot, an equation graphing program, and MatCalc, a matrix calculator program.

George Martin first became known to Fractint users when he brought a modicum of order to the chaotic world of formula postings with his release of the Orgform program and formula compilation. George added if..else to the formula parser language for version 19.6. Among his other contributions are the ability to include formula, ifs, and lsystem entries in .par files, the scrolling of text in the Z and F2 screens, and new autokey commands.

George received an A.B. in Economics from Dartmouth College and a J.D from the University of Michigan. When not playing with Fractint, he practices law in a small village about 40 miles northwest of Detroit.

Robin Bussell began contributing to Fractint in rudimentary fashion with the autologmap routine and has been producing more and more complex interface enhancements as he gets better at what he refers to as 'this C programming lark'. He is always grateful for the help the rest of the team have given in smoothing the rough edges of the ingredients he adds to the soup and regards the evolver feature as his greatest achievement to date.

Robin had far too much fun at college in London to actually get any qualifications there and has since worked his way up from a workshop job fixing computers back in the final days of CP/M, via some interesting work with Transputers (an innovative British cpu that was designed to run in massively parallel configurations, and made a very good Mandlebrot set calculating machine when a few dozen or more were set to the task), through to his position of senior engineer for a third party suppport company where he spends his time travelling the south west of Britain sorting out peoples IT problems.

When not playing with computers Robin likes to relax by experimenting with kite powered traction and can often be found hurtling around the local beaches on the end of a few square metres of fabric and carbon fibre in various configurations.

Distribution of Iterated Dynamics

New versions of Iterated Dynamics are released through github, https://github.com/LegalizeAdulthood/iterated-dynamics, and make their way to other systems from that point. Id is available as a Windows MSI installer, a ZIP file containing binaries and as a source code ZIP file.

The latest version of the code can always be found on the github repository.

Contacting the Author

Communication with the author for development of the next version of Iterated Dynamics takes place through the github repository, https://github.com/LegalizeAdulthood/iterated-dynamics. From there you can file bugs, feature requests and so-on.

The current main author is Richard Thomson, who is the maintainer of the github repository. You can email him directly at legalize@xmission.com, but it is best to use github.

GIF Save File Format

The Save command stores screen images as GIF (Graphics Interchange Format) files. The Restore command loads a GIF image and reads extra information from the file to restore all the fractal parameters used to generate the image. This GIF89a version of the format allows the placement of application data within the file in a standard manner.

GIF was originally created by CompuServe, but it used a compression algorithm patented by Unisys in 1985. This led to patent licensing issues with the file format, but all patents relating to the proprietary compression used for GIF have expired as of 2004.

Other Fractal Programs

Capow by Rudy Rucker is a Windows program for exploring continuous valued cellular automata. Rudy’s original source code is on github here: https://github.com/rudyrucker/capow and a version that builds with current editions of Visual Studio (as of April, 2024) is here: https://github.com/legalizeadulthood/capow

Kalles-Fraktaler is a fractal renderer with SIMD and multithreading support. Download from https://fraktaler.mathr.co.uk/

ManpWIN is a Windows fractal generator derived from DOS FRACTINT with lots of additional features by Paul de Leeuw. You can download the latest release from his web site: https://www.deleeuw.com.au/; Paul has collaborated with Richard Thomson to put his source code on github at https://github.com/PaulTheLionHeart/manpwin.

Movie Maker 3D by Yann Le Bihan can create animations using frames rendered by Kalles-Fraktaler. http://www.chillheimer.de/kallesfraktaler/mmy/

XaoS is a program that specializes in fast, fluid, continuous zooming. https://xaos-project.github.io/

Bibliography

Barnsley, Michael: "Fractals Everywhere", Academic Press, 1988.

Davenport, Clyde: "A Hypercomplex Calculus with Applications to Relativity", ISBN 0-9623837-0-8. This self-published expansion of Mr. Davenport’s Master’s thesis makes the case for using hypercomplex numbers rather than quaternions. This book provided the background for Id’s implementation of hypercomplex fractals.

Dewdney, A. K., "Computer Recreations" columns in "Scientific American"  — 8/85, 7/87, 11/87, 12/88, 7/89.

Devaney, Robert L., "An Introduction to Chaotic Dynamical Systems", Addison-Wesley, 1989. A detailed mathematical treatment of chaotic dynamical systems, assuming only a knowledge of calculus as a starting point.

Edgar, Gerald A.: "Classics on Fractals", Addison-Wesley, 1993. Collects papers related to fractals and the idea of fractional dimension that appeared before Benoit Mandelbrot first coined the term fractal in 1975.

Falconer, Kenneth: "Fractal Geometry", Wiley, 1990. Detailed treatement of the underlying mathematics of fractals, including excursions into topology and measure theory.

Feder, Jens: "Fractals", Plenum, 1988. Quite technical, with good coverage of applications in fluid percolation, game theory, and other areas.

Field, Michael and Golubitsky, Martin, "Symmetry in Chaos", Oxford University Press, 1992. A well illustrated book that introduced the "icon" fractal type.

Gleick, James: "Chaos: Making a New Science", Viking Press, 1987. The best non-technical account of the revolution in our understanding of dynamical systems and its connections with fractal geometry.

Mandelbrot, Benoit: "The Fractal Geometry of Nature", W. H. Freeman & Co., 1982. An even more revised and expanded version of the 1977 work. A rich and sometimes confusing stew of formal and informal mathematics, the prehistory of fractal geometry, and everything else. Best taken in small doses.

Mandelbrot, Benoit: "Fractals: Form, Chance, and Dimension", W. H. Freeman & Co., 1977. A much revised translation of "Les objets fractals: forme, hasard, et dimension", Flammarion, 1975.

Peitgen, Heinz-Otto & Richter, Peter: "The Beauty of Fractals", Springer-Verlag, 1986. THE coffee-table book of fractal images, knowledgeable on computer graphics as well as the mathematics they portray.

Peitgen, Heinz-Otto & Saupe, Ditmar: "The Science of Fractal Images", Springer-Verlag, 1988. A fantastic work, with a few nice pictures, but mostly filled with equations!!!

Pickover, Clifford: "Computers, Pattern, Chaos, and Beauty", St. Martin’s Press, 1990.

Schroeder, Manfred: "Fractals, Chaos, Power Laws", W. H. Freeman & Co., 1991.

Sprott, Julien C., "Strange Attractors", M & T Books, 1993. This is available online as a PDF: https://sprott.physics.wisc.edu/fractals/booktext/SABOOK.PDF

Thompson, J. M. T. and Stewart, H. B.: "Nonlinear Dynamics and Chaos", Wiley, 1986. Detailed discussion of nonlinear dynamical systems, bifurcation points and attractors. Discusses the Henon map, Rossler’s band and the Lorenz attractor.

Viscek, Tamas: "Fractal Growth Phenomena", World Scientific, 1989. Discusses diffusion-limited aggregation, cluster-cluster aggregation and other models of growth of structures and their fractal properties.

Revision History

Version 1.2

Version 1.2 is mostly a code cleanup release that removes integer fractal types and replaces them exclusively with floating-point types. This change was made to simplify the existing code paths in preparation for migration to wxWidgets in version 2.0.

Many thanks to Paul de Leeuw in helping us find a bunch of bugs that we fixed for this release!

New Features in Version 1.2

  • Native Windows file browse dialog for opening files.

  • Improved version handling with the reset parameter.

  • Improved version handling when reading GIF files.

  • Improved version handling when writing GIF files.

  • Improved rendering of mathematics in the HTML help.

When prompting the user to locate a file, Id now uses the native Windows Open File dialog. This replaces a bunch of homebrew code for locating a file under DOS using the full screen choice mechanism on the text screens. There are likely more filesystem related issues that need to be cleaned up; see issue #268.

Version Handling in Version 1.2 Onward

Previous versions of Iterated Dynamics reset the version to 1.0 in a breaking change from the legacy DOS FRACTINT version numbering. While this properly served to indicate the reality of Id being a fork from DOS FRACTINT, it created some interopability problems with parameter sets and image files between the two programs.

When creating a parameter file, the reset parameter is now written as reset=major/minor/patch/tweak. The major and minor version components are always written. The patch and tweak components appear if either component is non-zero. Legacy FRACTINT version numbers, such as reset=2004, when read from a parameter set are all treated as version 1.0 of Id for the purposes of backward compatibility.

Currently, no backwards compatibility with old FRACTINT behavior is applied to parameter sets. Legacy DOS FRACTINT parameter sets that rely on the reset parameter to have behavior adjusted may not render identical images in Id. Such parameter sets can be upgraded by loading the parameter set into DOS FRACTINT and either saving an image or creating a new parameter set in DOS FRACTINT.

When reading an image file, integer fractal types are converted to their corresponding floating-point fractal type. Legacy FRACTINT version numbers in image files are used to migrate legacy FRACTINT behavior to the current behavior in Id.

When writing an image file, Id writes the full major/minor/patch/tweak version number into the file and writes a legacy FRACTINT version number of 20.04. Such files may load in DOS FRACTINT, but no guarantees of compatibility with DOS FRACTINT are made.

Bugs Fixed in Version 1.2

  • Id will search standard locations for images specified on the command- line: current directory, savedir parameter location, and FRACTDIR environment variable location. (Fixes #267)

  • Id could overwrite image files in separate sessions, even when the overwrite parameter was not set. Id now properly checks for the existence of a file in the save location. (Fixes #264)

  • File system errors are now properly reported when writing image parameters. (Fixes #231)

  • The orbitname parameter for julibrot types is now documented. (Fixes #238)

  • The chip, quadruptwo and threeply types documentation was improved. (Fixes #252)

  • Versions 1.0, 1.1 and 1.1.1 wrote a version number into image files that was not compatible with loading into legacy DOS FRACTINT. That has been corrected.

Code Cleanup in Version 1.2

  • All integer fractal code paths and associated data have been removed.

  • A bunch of legacy FRACTINT files were removed from the repository. The remaining files were moved to a directory named 'legacy'.

  • Leftover files from the Sphinx version of HTML help have been removed.

  • More magic value integers were replaced with symbolic constants as enumerations.

New Features in Version 1.1:

  • Ctrl + and - can now be used to rotate the zoom box, in addition to the numeric keypad + and - keys. Some laptops don’t have a numeric keypad.

  • Perturbation drawing algorithm. Paul de Leeuw contributed an implementation of the perturbation drawing algorithm with support for the Mandelbrot (type=mandel) and Mandelbrot power (type=manzpower) fractal types. See Drawing Method and Perturbation Algorithm for details. (PR #160)

  • Configuration files 'sstools.ini' and 'id.cfg' can now be loaded from outside the installation directory. The following locations are searched in this order: user’s Documents directory, FRACTDIR environment variable location and then current directory. The directory related parameter values do not change this search order. When video mode key assignments are changed interactively, the updated id.cfg is written to the location specified by the savedir parameter, defaulting to the user’s Documents directory. Changing function key assignments while selecting video modes saves the updated id.cfg file to the savedir, defaulting to the user’s Documents directory. (Fixes #170)

  • Mouse support for the zoom box has been restored. (Fixes #14, #152)

  • Mouse support for the Orbits Window has been restored.

  • Mouse support for the inverse Julia set cursor has been restored. (Fixes #151)

  • The color palette editor can be positioned using the mouse and the current pixel whose color is displayed in the editor can also be selected with the mouse. (Fixes #150)

  • Disk video rendering performance and robustness improved. Requested memory buffers are now unlimited in disk video mode and only fall back to using a disk file if memory allocation fails. The operating system’s virtual memory will perform better than manual disk caches. Disk cache files are unique per-process, allowing multiple instances of Id to be running simultaneously without interfering with each other. The the status screen will now update at most ten times per second. This prevents GUI updates from being the bottleneck on disk video rendering. (Fixes #173, #174)

Bugs Fixed in Version 1.1:

  • When selecting a formula, L-system or IFS fractal type and the item is wide and/or needs scrolling, such as the Fractint entry of example2.frm, the surrounding box was improperly displayed. (Fixes #182)

  • The makepar parameter, or B commnd, now saves any generated parameter and batch files to the savedir location. (Fixes #176, #177)

  • Generated parameter file comments now properly handle escaped backslashes preceding another special character. (Fixes #175)

  • The version number is now correctly displayed in the title of help screens. (Fixes #154)

  • When run from the Visual Studio debugger, the working directory of the program is properly set to the home directory. (Fixes #153)

  • Corrected an assert popup during a Debug build. (Fixes #147, #140)

  • When the monitor configuration changed since the last time Id was run and the previous window position is no longer on-screen, the previous window position is forgotten and the window is placed by the system. (Fixes #136)

  • On Windows, crash dump files are saved to the savedir location. (Fixes #133)

  • When changing fractal types, if the the fractal parameters screen or entry name screen (for formula, ifs or L-system fractal types) were cancelled, the previous fractal type and associated parameters were lost. Now, canceling those screens restores the previous state. (Fixes #129)

Code Cleanup in Version 1.1:

  • Code style guide created to assist contributors. (Fixes #166)

  • More unit tests added, when reasonable, to prove buggy behavior and validate their fixes.

  • Library libid source and header files organized into subdirectories by role: 3d, engine, fractals, io, math, misc and ui.

  • test-id unit tests files organized into subdirectories, matching the function or file they test.

  • Identifier names renamed to conform to style guide.

  • Names of files updated to conform to style guide.

  • Calls to standard library functions qualified with namespace std to conform to style guide.

  • All platform (e.g. linux vs. Windows) variations isolated to CMake checks in the config library.

  • All calls to stricmp, strnicmp, and strncasecmp replaced with string_case_compare and string_case_equal from config library.

  • Platform driver types selected by config library in driver_types.h.

  • Platform file descriptor I/O header selected by config library in fdio.h.

  • Platform filelength function selected by config library in filelength.h.

  • Platform getpid function selected by config library in getpid.h.

  • Platform path limits selected by config library in path_limits.h.

  • All XFRACT conditionally compiled code eliminated by using config library.

  • Many more small improvements, see the git commit history for details.

Version 1.0

  • Fork of Fractint 20.04 patch level 4

  • New formula file MandelbrotDerivatives.frm with Burning Ship, Perpendicular Mandelbrot, Heart Mandelbrot, Mandelbar and other Mandelbrot set formula variations. The parameter file BurningShip.par provides example parameters for these variations. Contributed by Paul de Leeuw.

  • New $cpu$ comment variable expands to a description of your CPU.

  • Long filenames are now supported throughout.

  • All filename parameters are now case sensitive.

  • When browsing for files, e.g. Restoring *.GIF files, filenames are compared case insensitive against wildcard search masks.

  • Added new fractal types Mandelbrot Mix 4 and DivideBrot5 by Jim Muth. DivideBrot5 has arbitrary precision (AP) math support. Note that image skewing and inversion are not supported by the AP math routines. See Arbitrary Precision and Deep Zooming for other features not supported.

  • The orbitsavename parameter was added to specify the name of the raw orbits file. The orbits file, if it exists, is overwritten when overwrite=yes. Otherwise, the value of orbitsavename is incremented until a filename is formed that does not exist.

  • The autokeyname parameter was enhanced to create a unique filename when autokey=record unless overwrite=yes is specified.

  • Disk video buffer sizes were dramatically increased.

  • The formula parser has been enhanced to remove internal size limitations. The only limit on formula parsing is available memory.

  • The savedir parameter was added to specify the default directory used for writing any files. Since a Windows program is typically installed to the Program Files directory, which is read-only, it cannot be assumed that Id can write to the directory in which it is located.

Additional changes in Version 1.0:

  • Most of the changes involve internal restructuring of the DOS Fractint code to build a bridge to the future.

  • Iterated Dynamics is a native 64-bit Windows program written in C++ with a CMake build system and vcpkg for obtaining 3rd party library dependencies.

  • All assembly language code has been removed and, where practical, replaced with C++ code that performs the same function.

  • A CGA text display is simulated for all prompt screens and help screens.

  • A "video mode" determines the resolution of all saved images and is provided by a driver. Iterated Dynamics comes with two drivers: Disk and GDI. The GDI driver renders to the screen through the Windows GDI interface. The disk driver can be used to render images larger than your physical screen, but still uses your screen’s GUI for displaying status with a CGA style window.

  • Id.cfg, which defines the default video modes, was updated to remove all modes smaller than 800x600 and very large disk video modes were added.

  • DOS related information in video modes was dropped.

  • All online help text has been reviewed and revised to drop DOS specific discussions. Where still appropriate the text has been updated to reflect that Id is a program operating in a windowed environment.

  • The release parameter resets all values to their default but does not enable any backwards compatible behavior in this release. For backward compatability with old behavior, use Fractint.

  • The monitorwidth parameter was renamed to stereowidth. The old parameter name is still accepted but will be deprecated in a future release.

  • Printing an image has been removed. Use your operating system for that. :)

  • The following parameter file commands are deprecated and support will be removed in a future release. In this release the arguments are parsed and validated and the results ignored. adapter halftone ramvideo afi iterincr rleps biospalette linefeed textsafe colorps maxcolorres title comport noninterlaced tplus epsf pixelzoom translate exitmode plotstyle tweaklzw fpu printer vesadetect gif87a printfile
